  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5eece331-b3c6-48f3-a7e6-4a0e7f0595ea'
      });

  <span id="freeText11154599779199168821" style="display:none">17 year-old Haley McWaid is a good girl, the pride of her suburban New Jersey family, captain of the lacrosse team, headed off to college next year with all the hopes and dreams her doting parents can pin on her. Which is why, when her mother wakes one morning to find that Haley never came home the night before, and three months quickly pass without word from the girl, the community assumes the worst.<br /><br />Wendy Tynes is a reporter on a mission, to identify and bring down sexual predators via elaborate—and nationally televised—sting operations. Working with local police on her news program Caught in the Act, Wendy and her team have publicly shamed dozens of men by the time she encounters her latest target. Dan Mercer is a social worker known as a friend to troubled teens, but his story soon becomes more complicated than Wendy could have imagined.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_8264697').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_8264697').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_8264697').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1957019347" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1957019347" />
    <a title="Mandy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30940542-mandy"><img alt="Mandy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596388463p2/30940542.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1957019347?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mandy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mandy" href="/user/show/30940542-mandy">Mandy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780451232700" href="/book/show/8264697-caught">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1957019347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9275106596275606413">It was hard not to get "caught" up in this novel (excuse my corny pun). If you haven't read a Coben novel you're missing out. This guy can write books like no one's business. He is to mystery writing as Reba is to country music. Coben is one of the best, if not THE BEST mystery authors out there. My life goal is to read all his books! :) his books are my happy place!<br/><br/>This book was another one of his that had twists and turns and at the very end knocks you back and does a one eighty and I FREAKING</span>
  <span id="freeText9275106596275606413" style="display:none">It was hard not to get "caught" up in this novel (excuse my corny pun). If you haven't read a Coben novel you're missing out. This guy can write books like no one's business. He is to mystery writing as Reba is to country music. Coben is one of the best, if not THE BEST mystery authors out there. My life goal is to read all his books! :) his books are my happy place!<br /><br />This book was another one of his that had twists and turns and at the very end knocks you back and does a one eighty and I FREAKING LOVE THAT! <br /><br />In the beginning of this Dan Mercer goes to a house with a red door.... and after he opens it he can't shut it. His life spirals out of control as does everyone else's that is somewhat associated with him. Wendy Tynes, a high-profile reporter is who was behind that door... she has something on Dan but Dan says he's innocent... but is he?<br /><br />From there, Harlan Coben takes you down a yellow brick road that even Dorothy would be confused on. Everything from scandals to murder, to a missing teenager that seems to have nothing to do with the plot, enters the story and it will keep you on the edge of your seat until the very last page. <br /><br />Harlan's books make me want to sit down and read them and try as I might I can never figure out his ending, he ALWAYS throws me a curve ball, but that is why I love him!<br /><br />Highly recommend! I will probably always recommend a Coben! :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9275106596275606413" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/97813896?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle♥" href="/user/show/2607921-michelle">Michelle♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2607921-michelle?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2607921-michelle?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97813896" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14218312783261774413">There were two parts to this book. Mind you, I have been anxiously waiting for Coben to come out with a new book. I absolutely love him and think he might be my favorite author of all time.<br/><br/>I always get wrapped up and into the story and literally finish his book within a day or less, and that was the case with this one. Like I said there were two parts to this book.<br/><br/>It kind of threw me because I'm not used to that style of writing from him. There was the dark anticipation and then it spun you for </span>
  <span id="freeText14218312783261774413" style="display:none">There were two parts to this book. Mind you, I have been anxiously waiting for Coben to come out with a new book. I absolutely love him and think he might be my favorite author of all time.<br /><br />I always get wrapped up and into the story and literally finish his book within a day or less, and that was the case with this one. Like I said there were two parts to this book.<br /><br />It kind of threw me because I'm not used to that style of writing from him. There was the dark anticipation and then it spun you for a whirlwind.<br /><br />I do not want to give away any details from the book, but this was just a little too far-fetched for me. Pedophiles, kidnapping, facebook, one annoying "reporter". I don't know.<br /><br />The only thing I truly liked about this book was the fact that Win made an appearance. (I have a secret love crush on him. He's from the Myron Bolitar series.)<br /><br />For me, this book didn't do Coben justice. It was not what I thought it was going to be, then again his twists and turns never are. But this was just TOO far-fetched this time.<br /><br />One of the best quotes from the book that made me literally laugh out loud and say "so true!" was on page 319:<br /><br />"I remember one time I heard this English professor asking the class what the world's scariest noise is. Is it a man crying out in pain? A woman's scream of terror? A gunshot? A baby crying? And the professor shakes his head and says, 'No, the scariest noise is, you're all alone in your dark empty house, you KNOW you're all alone, you know that there is NO chance anyone else is home or within MILES - and then, suddenly, from upstairs, you hear the toliet flush.'"</span>
  <a data-text-id="14218312783261774413" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Told in multiple POV, 3rd person, it’s a standalone novel. It was a bit dark, a bit slow for my taste, unpredictable with a shocking ending and satisfying! Overall, it was a good read and hope you enjoy it as well!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5794294273856959750">Wow! When you read this one you will need to take notes, create a flow chart, etc. and I bet you still won't see anything coming. Not only did keep thinking that I had guessed where the story was going, Coben had me convinced I was right and the BAM! nope . . . wrong again! This happened about 10 times. Only 4 stars because it didn't blow me away, but it was very good.<br/><br/>Also, the mid-life crisis men's club was pretty funny. And, bonus appearance by Win from the Bolitar series.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_97410995" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/97410995" />
    <a title="Barbara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2172096-barbara"><img alt="Barbara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598060221p2/2172096.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/97410995?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbara" href="/user/show/2172096-barbara">Barbara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2172096-barbara?shelf=women-of-mystery-2017">women-of-mystery-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer97410995&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97410995" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1614013068852981690"><br/><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>WARNING: THIS REVIEW MIGHT CONTAIN (WHAT YOU CONSIDER) SPOILERS<br/><br/>Wendy Tynes is a television journalist for the program 'Caught in the Act', a show that lures in and exposes child predators. Dan Mercer, a divorced Princeton graduate who coaches troubled kids, is ensnared by Wendy's machinations and accused of targeting a young girl. However, the evidence is compromised and a judge lets Mercer off. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563974507i/27878949.jpg' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This infuriates Ed Grayson - whose son was abused - and he shoots and kills Mercer right in </span>
  <span id="freeText1614013068852981690" style="display:none"><br><b>3.5 stars</b><br><br>WARNING: THIS REVIEW MIGHT CONTAIN (WHAT YOU CONSIDER) SPOILERS<br><br>Wendy Tynes is a television journalist for the program 'Caught in the Act', a show that lures in and exposes child predators. Dan Mercer, a divorced Princeton graduate who coaches troubled kids, is ensnared by Wendy's machinations and accused of targeting a young girl. However, the evidence is compromised and a judge lets Mercer off. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563974507i/27878949.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This infuriates Ed Grayson - whose son was abused - and he shoots and kills Mercer right in front of Wendy. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563974507i/27878951.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>However Grayson is a former U.S. Marshall - and a very clever guy - who gets rid of the body, obfuscates the evidence, and hires top-notch criminal defense attorney Hester Crimstein. Thus, it looks like Grayson can't even be brought to trial. And even if he could be, the jury would more likely congratulate him than convict him.<br><br>Meanwhile, a 17-year-old high school girl named Haley McWaid has been missing for three months.....and new evidence points to Mercer (now dead) as the possible abductor. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563974507i/27878952.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There's a problem though. Wendy's been re-examining the evidence that Mercer was a pedophile and - in retrospect - it looks inconclusive. Hence, Wendy fears she may have 'outed' an innocent man.....and indirectly got him killed. Moreover, Wendy's not positive Mercer was involved in Haley's disappearance either. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563974507i/27878947.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Wendy's guilty conscience leads her to delve into Mercer's life, going all the way back to his years at Princeton. And lo and behold, Wendy discovers that something bad happened at the Ivy League University a couple of decades back.....something that might be connected to what's occurring now. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563974507i/27878948.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>As Wendy's trying to uncover the truth she interviews Mercer's family and friends, some of whom have lost lucrative jobs because of the economy. One of Mercer's unemployed buddies - who's fashioned himself into a rapper called Tenafly - provides some comic relief from the darker parts of the story. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563974507i/27878950.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Wendy's investigation, helped by playboy/tycoon Windsor Horne Lockwood III (Win)- eventually leads her to the truth.....which is quite twisty and surprising. <br><br>Two themes in the book are revenge and forgiveness. Terrible wrongs have been done to some characters, and the issue of whether to forgive or not arises several times. To me the forgiveness motif didn't meld smoothly into the story and felt awkward. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563974507i/27878953.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>All in all I liked the book pretty well, and it was fun to see Hester Crimstein and Win - who are recurring characters in Coben's books. I think most mystery fans would enjoy 'Caught' and recommend the book to them. <br><br>You can follow my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot.com/">http://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1614013068852981690" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1258529127?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<div id="review_1622421507" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1622421507" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1622421507?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Thriller fans who don't want to think too hard. </span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1622421507" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16871978322901938372">I usually cannot stand books with characters who're idiots or plots that rely on those characters being idiots, but this one wasn't so bad. In fact, I had a damn good time. I've met single-cell organisms with more going on upstairs than reporter and all around doofus Wendy, but Harlan Coben made her extremely easy to read about. There's no way she could've put any of the ending together by herself, but the journey was twisty enough that it kept my attention. <br/><br/>Oh, and I know Coben has a long-runni</span>
  <span id="freeText16871978322901938372" style="display:none">I usually cannot stand books with characters who're idiots or plots that rely on those characters being idiots, but this one wasn't so bad. In fact, I had a damn good time. I've met single-cell organisms with more going on upstairs than reporter and all around doofus Wendy, but Harlan Coben made her extremely easy to read about. There's no way she could've put any of the ending together by herself, but the journey was twisty enough that it kept my attention. <br /><br />Oh, and I know Coben has a long-running series, but it was refreshing to read a thriller that wasn't part of a fucking series. <br /><br />I made several updates while reading this book. I said I knew who Chynna was. I was wrong. I said I knew everything about Dan Mercer. I was, again, very wrong. In fact, the only thing I was right about what the level of stupidity of the characters. The plot was convoluted, but not in a bad way. I had to suspend my disbelief once or twice (more on that in the Spoiler Discussion), but what story doesn't call for a bit of suspension? <br /><br />In summation: No reason you won't enjoy reading this one. If nothing else, it's a fine way to blow a dozen hours, that is, if you're slow reader like me. Someone like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys" rel="nofollow noopener">Shelbs</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar" rel="nofollow noopener">Kells</a> would likely read this in an hour or so. <br /><br />Final Judgment: Stupid is as stupid does, but, here, stupid is sure fun to watch.<br /><br />Spoiler Discussion: Wherein I spoil <i>Caught</i>, by Harlan Coben.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br />So I am to believe that after this girl died of alcohol poisoning in Jenna's house that Jenna kept the girl's cell phone? She went through all that trouble to bury the body way out in the middle of nowhere, but she held onto a cell phone, which she later used to frame her ex-husband. Mind you, she had no idea she would ever need the cell phone. It was just a great coincidence that the need for it arose... Riiiiiiiiiiiight...<br /><br />Who the fuck hears "hunt" and "college students" and doesn't automatically think SCAVENGER HUNT! Fuck off. Wendy's bumbling ass couldn't figure that out? Come on. This lady was oblivious throughout the entire book, and I'm supposed to believe she figured everything out in the end? Nope. Not buying it. <br /><br />All that white rapper nonsense was awkward. I know Harlan Coben meant for it to be awkward, but there's no way this Ten-A-Fly guy had any fans with those lyrics. He was worse than Jamie Kennedy's character in <i>Malibu's Most Wanted</i>. <br /><br />Thanks for joining me. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="16871978322901938372" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_152005789" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/152005789" />
    <a title="Daniel Audet" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4411850-daniel-audet"><img alt="Daniel Audet" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286996074p2/4411850.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/152005789?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel Audet" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel Audet" href="/user/show/4411850-daniel-audet">Daniel Audet</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer152005789" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11039415382037236007">I finished this book yesterday and as I read the last few lines I couldn't help remarking to myself that this had to be Coben's best one yet. The pacing was break neck, the characters though all different and some as dysfunctional as a human can get - were believable, some even sympathetic, and some NOT, which is as it should be. Our heroine is an investigative news reporter and a single mom who gets embroiled in job related issues (not good ones) and a murder mystery involving a major college, </span>
  <span id="freeText11039415382037236007" style="display:none">I finished this book yesterday and as I read the last few lines I couldn't help remarking to myself that this had to be Coben's best one yet. The pacing was break neck, the characters though all different and some as dysfunctional as a human can get - were believable, some even sympathetic, and some NOT, which is as it should be. Our heroine is an investigative news reporter and a single mom who gets embroiled in job related issues (not good ones) and a murder mystery involving a major college, it's alumni, leaders in the community, the feds and local cops, the internet (good social media and techie detail here too), and predators of young girls. As a "plot' this one has it all. Sub-plots to die for, story arcs only a major leaguer like Coben could pull off, just enough narration and description to keep you on the edge of your seat and guessing WHO. I read a lot of mysteries and I gotta' tell ya', Harlan had me wondering until the end. You think you have it figured out and he throws you a 100 mile-an-hour curve ball, bang you're back to zero with no choice but to read on. Only someone with this authors skills could make the suburbs the deepest darkest jungle of the human soul, rip it from the headlines and kick your ass with it. You'll question your own values in areas of your mind, heart and spirit and like the characters in this killer thriller you WILL make choices, choices to live by that stay with you like this book will. Whatever genre you like to read or write in, I can't recommend this book enough. At 388 pages it reads as quick as a short story but you'll be glad it's not. Harlan Coben is at the top of his game with this one fiction fans. I very much look forward to his next release. He's on Twitter too: as @HarlanCoben - <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://twitter.com/harlancoben">http://twitter.com/harlancoben</a><br />_______________________________________________________________________________________________________<br />I was able to get my hands on Caught by major leaguer Harlan Coben so I'm slotting the reading of it before Kristin Kimball's non-fiction book The Dirty Life. This story, so far, and I'm just a dozen or so pages in, has the pacing and intrigue hints I love about Coben's work. I've read several of his books over the last few years and I'm sure this one will be a great ride. More soon as I dive into this story of a girl who disappears, the reasons WHY and the dirty little secrets revealed in a town, that tell us a bit about ourselves, and some among us, that we may not want to face. But we will.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11039415382037236007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2598535196" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14566691385008063555"><b>April2020</b> Reading with Action/Adventure Aficionados group here:<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/21301573'>https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/...</a><br/><br/>This was an excellent read again, although I kind of knew what was coming. The first time was better, but this time I could appreciate the foreshadowing & clues better. I've also read most of the Myron Bolivar series, so I appreciated Win more.<br/><br/><b>Nov2018</b>The first book I read by him was <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/215238.Play_Dead' title='Play Dead by Harlan Coben' rel='nofollow noopener'>Play Dead</a>, the first he published & it wasn't that great. This author was recommended by my dentist, so I gave hi</span>
  <span id="freeText14566691385008063555" style="display:none"><b>April2020</b> Reading with Action/Adventure Aficionados group here:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/21301573">https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/...</a><br /><br />This was an excellent read again, although I kind of knew what was coming. The first time was better, but this time I could appreciate the foreshadowing &amp; clues better. I've also read most of the Myron Bolivar series, so I appreciated Win more.<br /><br /><b>Nov2018</b>The first book I read by him was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/215238.Play_Dead" title="Play Dead by Harlan Coben" rel="nofollow noopener">Play Dead</a>, the first he published &amp; it wasn't that great. This author was recommended by my dentist, so I gave him another shot. Then I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/157320.Mystery_Writers_of_America_Presents_Death_Do_Us_Part_New_Stories_about_Love__Lust__and_Murder" title="Mystery Writers of America Presents Death Do Us Part New Stories about Love, Lust, and Murder by Harlan Coben" rel="nofollow noopener">Mystery Writers of America Presents Death Do Us Part: New Stories about Love, Lust, and Murder</a> which he edited &amp; wrote the final story in. It was one of the better short story collections, so I thought I'd give him another try &amp; I'm glad I did.<br /><br />The main theme of trial by public opinion was superbly done. I hate to see public postings of arrests since it assumes guilt before trial. In the case of child molestation, it is especially damaging. All it takes is a believable false accusation to completely ruin a person. I was appalled the show <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/To_Catch_a_Predator" rel="nofollow noopener">To Catch A Predator</a> since it smacks of entrapment that is all too easily spoofed. That the show was so popular just proves a decadence in our society, a craving for blood &amp; circuses. <br /><br />I can't recall when I've read a twistier mystery. New bits of information kept coming all the way until the very end that changed the context of the story &amp; the characters from good guys to villains to people who made good or bad decisions &amp; then just got caught up. Excellent foreshadowing this time, too. Wow, what a ride!<br /><br />There were quite a few false notes peppered throughout the story. No big ones this time, but a number of irritating ones. Most turned out to be part of the twisty story &amp; the heroine picked up on them eventually. The biggest issue I had was that she was supposed to be so good at being an investigative reporter, yet she kept missing &amp; forgetting things. I kept muttering that she should take notes if her memory was that bad, but 2 friends told me they didn't catch these issues either.<br /><br />The book was very well narrated &amp; I'll definitely look for more by him.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14566691385008063555" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Seemingly normal people hiding some very dark secrets. I have seen a few of the Dateline - To Catch a Predator episodes so I found that story-line quite interesting.   <span id="freeText4230829520046474233" style="display:none">I read this book while on holiday last year and really enjoyed it. <br /><br />Quite a few stories intertwining but focusing primarily on a missing girl and a TV program that carries out live child predator stings. Seemingly normal people hiding some very dark secrets. I have seen a few of the Dateline - To Catch a Predator episodes so I found that story-line quite interesting. There were times I wondered if perhaps the show had read the situation wrong (however unlikely). A person who may in fact be innocent can have their lives irrevocably damaged just by the accusation. <br /><br />I enjoyed the multiple story-lines and many characters. Full of twists, lies, and shocking revelations. Though not always realistic still entertaining. With all of the different events going on I definitely had to pay close attention but for the most part I could keep up. <br />"Caught" is very fast paced with interesting story-lines and many dysfunctional yet entertaining characters. <br /><br />Harlan Coben has a way of pulling you in and not letting go until the last page.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1220267200" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1220267200" />
    <a title="Jean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28831526-jean"><img alt="Jean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579801852p2/28831526.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1220267200?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jean" href="/user/show/28831526-jean">Jean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1220267200" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4170429760254480381"><i>“I knew opening that red door would destroy my life.”</i> Those are the opening words of Harlan Coben’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6681454.Caught' title='Caught by Harlan Coben' rel='nofollow noopener'>Caught</a>. Dan Mercer, a dedicated child social worker, is caught in a TV sting operation by Wendy Tynes, a reporter who has made a career of taping and broadcasting supposed pedophiles caught in the act. <br/><br/>Wendy comes off as pretty stereotypical at first, like a female reporter who has no scruples. As the story progresses, however, she seems to find her conscience. Dan claims that he was set up, and W</span>
  <span id="freeText4170429760254480381" style="display:none"><i>“I knew opening that red door would destroy my life.”</i> Those are the opening words of Harlan Coben’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6681454.Caught" title="Caught by Harlan Coben" rel="nofollow noopener">Caught</a>. Dan Mercer, a dedicated child social worker, is caught in a TV sting operation by Wendy Tynes, a reporter who has made a career of taping and broadcasting supposed pedophiles caught in the act. <br /><br />Wendy comes off as pretty stereotypical at first, like a female reporter who has no scruples. As the story progresses, however, she seems to find her conscience. Dan claims that he was set up, and Wendy wonders if perhaps Dan really was innocent. Dan is an enigma. I didn’t know what to make of Dan through most of the book. Before long, things become, much more complicated than just Dan’s pedophilia charge.<br /><br />As the story progresses, it may very well be the reader who is caught. The plot races from Dan to his ex- wife to a missing high school girl to Dan’s college buddies to, back and forth, all with Wendy in the middle. I found this book to be filled with lies, deceit, and characters I wasn’t quite sure I liked but didn’t exactly hate.<br /><br />While I’ve read much better books, I enjoyed the story telling, and this book was quite a ride. There are folks in this tale who learn some hard lessons. There is also some stuff that is pretty unrealistic. I did get a few laughs at the sarcasm, but the attitude of the lawyers was over the top. All in all, though, I was happy to be caught up in Coben’s <i>Caught</i> for a day.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4170429760254480381" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_106438075" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/106438075" />
    <a title="miteypen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/970590-miteypen"><img alt="miteypen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547377462p2/970590.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/106438075?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="miteypen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="miteypen" href="/user/show/970590-miteypen">miteypen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer106438075" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5643271051078563171">Not one of Coben's best. For one thing, a character who speaks in the first person in the prologue immediately fades into the background after I had become intrigued by his story. I think it would have been stronger if he had been the protagonist, a man trying to get out of his own predicament. Instead, Coben switches to a new character and I couldn't quite get into her. (For one thing, the book changes from first person to third.) He briefly introduces a character from other books of his, but t</span>
  <span id="freeText5643271051078563171" style="display:none">Not one of Coben's best. For one thing, a character who speaks in the first person in the prologue immediately fades into the background after I had become intrigued by his story. I think it would have been stronger if he had been the protagonist, a man trying to get out of his own predicament. Instead, Coben switches to a new character and I couldn't quite get into her. (For one thing, the book changes from first person to third.) He briefly introduces a character from other books of his, but that's unsatisfying, too, because he's a rather colorful character and here he's only given a bit part. In this book, he served only as an easy way for the main character to get information that she would have had trouble getting otherwise. <br /><br />That was the main weakness of the book: the mystery (there was actually more than one) was convoluted and the main character solved it/them without the reader being able to see all her thought processes or problem-solving actions. She just suddenly "knows." I don't usually care whether I figure the mystery out on my own, but I like to have more clues along the way. <br /><br />Not exactly a waste of time (it was a quick read), but I certainly wouldn't recommend it as an introduction to Harlan Coben's work. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5643271051078563171" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText18426753925860228910" style="display:none">Wow! I had to take so many notes with this one and by the end I had to go back a bit until I had it figured out. Just when you think it's gonna go in one direction, instead it goes in the exact opposite! <br /><br />Caught is about Reporter Wendy Tynes, who is making a living by bringing down sexual predators on TV sting operations. When one who is accused of being a pedophile and is tied to the disappearance of a seventeen-year old girl, Wendy is drawn into a deadly mystery and discovering the choices of right and wrong.<br /><br />The story also has a good message about forgiveness, to forgive others for their actions and to also forgive yourself. <br /><br />A great plot, great story, great characters, and most of all, A GREAT WRITER!!<br /><br />PS, I also forgot to mention that Win (Windsor Horne Lockwood) from the Myron Bolitar series (also by Harlan Coben) makes a cameo appearance in Caught, which I thought was pretty cool!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18426753925860228910" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_102317292" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102317292" />
    <a title="Linda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1050198-linda"><img alt="Linda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442423160p2/1050198.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/102317292?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda" href="/user/show/1050198-linda">Linda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1050198-linda?shelf=mystery-crime">mystery-crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer102317292&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102317292" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17073676301112888912">Harlan Coben takes on the issue of vigilantism in this story about a high profile TV reporter, Wendy Tynes, who entraps men suspected of being child molesters. Wendy has been successful with these ploys until she catches one Dan Mercer, who protests his innocence and is acquitted, only to find himself the target of outraged parents. After all, everyone now knows he’s a pedophile. Wendy is fired, and devotes herself to further investigation when Dan is murdered. This promises to be an engaging pl</span>
  <span id="freeText17073676301112888912" style="display:none">Harlan Coben takes on the issue of vigilantism in this story about a high profile TV reporter, Wendy Tynes, who entraps men suspected of being child molesters. Wendy has been successful with these ploys until she catches one Dan Mercer, who protests his innocence and is acquitted, only to find himself the target of outraged parents. After all, everyone now knows he’s a pedophile. Wendy is fired, and devotes herself to further investigation when Dan is murdered. This promises to be an engaging plot, but it becomes so complicated with a conglomeration of ancillary characters that the plot gets lost in the shuffle. Among these are a middle aged white rapper named “Ten-a-fly”, a missing teenager, a group of Princeton alums who keep getting involved in scandals, a TV judge, and the woman who killed Wendy’s husband in a DWI accident and who wants Wendy’s forgiveness. As a result, no one character, not even Wendy, is given much depth, and it’s difficult to care about what happens to any of them. The point of all this is that Wendy may indeed be guilty of fingering an innocent man, and she longs for his forgiveness, and she must reconcile her anger at the drunk driver with her guilt over her mistaken judgment. This is an honorable theme, but Coben takes his readers all around Robin Hood’s barn to get there.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17073676301112888912" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95606009" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13288851969230578748">It really does not need to be said that this was an excellent read. One should only look at who the author is and then immediately would know that they are in for a treat.<br/><br/>This book (like all of this author's books) really packs a punch from the first page until, literally, the very last page. As promised, the author delivers another WTF ending that leaves you with adrenaline pumping and dizzy from excitement.<br/><br/>I absolutely LOVED the main character Wendy Tynes, although I admit I was not digging he</span>
  <span id="freeText13288851969230578748" style="display:none">It really does not need to be said that this was an excellent read. One should only look at who the author is and then immediately would know that they are in for a treat.<br /><br />This book (like all of this author's books) really packs a punch from the first page until, literally, the very last page. As promised, the author delivers another WTF ending that leaves you with adrenaline pumping and dizzy from excitement.<br /><br />I absolutely LOVED the main character Wendy Tynes, although I admit I was not digging her at the get go. My first impression was that she was another self-centered, career-minded, don't care who I step on as I climb this very wobbly ladder, reporter. My impression changed swiftly as the plot unravels and my goodness does this plot unravel fast!<br /><br />I highly recommend this book to...well just about anyone. Those who are new to Harlan Coben, life-long fans, and those who are still left standing in the dark wondering where have all the good authors gone. Look no further.</span>

<div id="review_835649703" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/835649703" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3191832-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463550510p2/3191832.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/835649703?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/3191832-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer835649703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12372817393157018942">The only thing that saved this one from a one-star rating was the narrator. She was hilarious. You could hear it in her voice: I know this is ridiculous but I'm doing my best with it. She had to deliver the craziest lines and she did it with flair. She even had to rap as a 45 year old white guy who thinks he can fill a niche in the music business. The story itself was terrible. No suspense at all. Even though this was a pretty bad experience, I'm still going to give Tell No One a try, because it</span>
  <span id="freeText12372817393157018942" style="display:none">The only thing that saved this one from a one-star rating was the narrator. She was hilarious. You could hear it in her voice: I know this is ridiculous but I'm doing my best with it. She had to deliver the craziest lines and she did it with flair. She even had to rap as a 45 year old white guy who thinks he can fill a niche in the music business. The story itself was terrible. No suspense at all. Even though this was a pretty bad experience, I'm still going to give Tell No One a try, because it's gotten really good reviews from some really good readers. I think I may have just picked out the dud in the Coben bunch. Time will tell. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12372817393157018942" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_225674643" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/225674643" />
    <a title="Jenny Maloney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/854965-jenny-maloney"><img alt="Jenny Maloney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426173938p2/854965.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/225674643?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny Maloney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny Maloney" href="/user/show/854965-jenny-maloney">Jenny Maloney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/854965-jenny-maloney?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/854965-jenny-maloney?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/854965-jenny-maloney?shelf=violence">violence</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/854965-jenny-maloney?shelf=intrigue">intrigue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/854965-jenny-maloney?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/854965-jenny-maloney?shelf=sex">sex</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/854965-jenny-maloney?shelf=corporations">corporations</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer225674643" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10794983616532180278"><b>The Premise:</b> Reporter Wendy Tynes operates a <i>Dateline</i>-esque sting of a probable pedophile named Dan Mercer. He insists he's being set up. When the case against him is thrown out, she questions her conclusions. When she witnesses Mercer's murder...she's not sure what the hell is going on. Of course, as she digs deepers, the troubles (job loss, death threats, etc.) mount up. <br/><br/><b>The Big Issue:</b> This is one convaluted story, with subplots within subplots within subplots. While Coben walks a fine line he</span>
  <span id="freeText10794983616532180278" style="display:none"><b>The Premise:</b> Reporter Wendy Tynes operates a <i>Dateline</i>-esque sting of a probable pedophile named Dan Mercer. He insists he's being set up. When the case against him is thrown out, she questions her conclusions. When she witnesses Mercer's murder...she's not sure what the hell is going on. Of course, as she digs deepers, the troubles (job loss, death threats, etc.) mount up. <br /><br /><b>The Big Issue:</b> This is one convaluted story, with subplots within subplots within subplots. While Coben walks a fine line here, I think he <i>basically</i> pulls it off. Any of the plots/subplots separately would've made an interesting book - after all, most of them have graced the headlines of national newspapers. And, in my opinion, that's the weakness of the story. I can buy Wall Street traders ripping retirees out of their retirement. I can buy a reporter questioning her headlining pedophile story. I can buy shadowy figures out to seek revenge for any of the following: a child who has been abused, a man falsely accused, or kidnapping a teenager. I can buy a schizophrenic man holding the clues to everything in his broken psyche. <br /><br />Way harder to buy all of that in one novel. And, oh yes, the above situations are all in there, plus some that I haven't mentioned....But I'm not giving anything away. I'd have to rewrite the book in order for anyone reading here to understand the different levels going on. <br /><br />In the book's defense, however, the various layers - which make the story rather incoherent when you try to explain it to a stranger - do not let you put the book down. The pages keep turning. I finished this book in a one-page-turn-after-another day. But, if you're anything like me, you'll be left with a little tinge of: Really?<br /><br /><b>Lesser Issues (a.k.a. My Personal Pet Peeves):</b> The way technology is presented. For example, I don't buy for one <i>iota</i> of a second that any reporter - local, national, international, or alien - worth their salt (as main character Wendy is portrayed) does <i>not</i> have a Facebook account...or that they would not know, at the very least, how to use the world's largest networking site. And I'll leave it at that.<br /><br /><b>The Good Stuff:</b> The side characters rocked my world. I loved the "Fathers Club." I'm probably with the vast majority of the music business when I say that I don't think middle-aged white men should be trying to break into the rap sector, but as a reader I appreciated that Ten-a-Fly made the effort. (Yeah, I didn't list it above, but middle-aged-white-man-rapping is in this book too! Huzzah!) <br /><br />Some of the other reviewers have mentioned Win. Only a few pages, but he's there and he makes an impression.<br /><br />I adored the cartoony lawyers: Flair Hickory and the Judge Judy-esque Hester Crimstein. (Though I do have an issue with how Crimstein is portrayed as rather 'brilliant'. Mostly she was like a bulldog - any police department would've pushed charges with the evidence stacked against her client...so it struck me as strange that her questionable arguments had the cops in awe.)<br /><br /><b>Overall:</b> Enjoyed this one. It's a good, quick read with (literally) a million points of interest. Definitely worth your time if you're in the market for an entertaining weekend. <br /><br />~Jenny<br /><a href="http://www.placeforthestolen.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Place for the Stolen</a><br /><a href="http://www.undergroundwritingproject.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Under Ground Writing Project</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10794983616532180278" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_326896418" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/326896418" />
    <a title="Patrice Hoffman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5405898-patrice-hoffman"><img alt="Patrice Hoffman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545145717p2/5405898.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/326896418?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrice Hoffman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrice Hoffman" href="/user/show/5405898-patrice-hoffman">Patrice Hoffman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer326896418" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10103238471334985273">I enjoyed reading this Coben novel. It has all the same traits as any of this author's other books. There are twists, lies, and shocking revelations. Coben always manages to grip the reader from page one. <br/><br/>The story begins with Dan Mercer entering a house he suspects he really shouldn't be in. The red door is screaming at him to stop and turn the other way. Lo and hold, he's being setup by Wendy Tynes to be captured on video as a sexual predator. You know the NBC show "To Catch a Predator". Wendy</span>
  <span id="freeText10103238471334985273" style="display:none">I enjoyed reading this Coben novel. It has all the same traits as any of this author's other books. There are twists, lies, and shocking revelations. Coben always manages to grip the reader from page one. <br /><br />The story begins with Dan Mercer entering a house he suspects he really shouldn't be in. The red door is screaming at him to stop and turn the other way. Lo and hold, he's being setup by Wendy Tynes to be captured on video as a sexual predator. You know the NBC show "To Catch a Predator". Wendy is the host of the type of show. Dan Mercer is her latest predator/victim. The novel progresses on to findout if he's in fact the monster that he's being accused of being.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/24689.Harlan_Coben" title="Harlan Coben" rel="nofollow noopener">Harlan Coben</a> always manages to take the reader on twists and turns that are never seen coming. The writing is always easy and to the point. There are always a lot of characters that seemingly are just bystanders until they come into the forefront. That may also be the reason why the ones in this particular book are a little stale. When I want a good, fun , easy read the depth of the characters is not that important to me. I mean c'mon. It's a thriller for God's sake.<br /><br />Overall, this book is classic Coben. If you're a fan of Coben, you will enjoy this book. My only gripe is that after reading a few of his books, the formulaic ending is sometimes maddening. The first few times it's read you're like "Whoa" but after reading it so many more times, it's like "enough already!". Anyway, I did enjoy this book and can't wait to read the next one I have sitting on my shelf somewhere at home.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10103238471334985273" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_742180967" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/742180967" />
    <a title="Janie Johnson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5116650-janie-johnson"><img alt="Janie Johnson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486148700p2/5116650.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/742180967?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Janie Johnson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Janie Johnson" href="/user/show/5116650-janie-johnson">Janie Johnson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780451232700" href="/book/show/8264697-caught">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5116650-janie-johnson?shelf=2013-challenge">2013-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer742180967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7350830565078445475">I was looking forward to reading this book since I enjoyed the other two I have read so far by Coben. This book did not disappoint me, and I think I enjoyed even more than the ones I read before. Coben's writing style, to me, is in a class by itself when it comes to Mystery. And has everything I love about a good mystery. A great cast of characters, a great plot, fluidity, and a whole lot of mystery! I gotta say he kept me guessing throughout the whole book. Just when I thought something was mak</span>
  <span id="freeText7350830565078445475" style="display:none">I was looking forward to reading this book since I enjoyed the other two I have read so far by Coben. This book did not disappoint me, and I think I enjoyed even more than the ones I read before. Coben's writing style, to me, is in a class by itself when it comes to Mystery. And has everything I love about a good mystery. A great cast of characters, a great plot, fluidity, and a whole lot of mystery! I gotta say he kept me guessing throughout the whole book. Just when I thought something was making sense, and it was all figured out, something else came to the fore front!<br /><br />Imagine you are a reporter and you have a show where you are bringing down sexual predators to help keep our kids safe, and then you trap someone who totally makes you second guess your instinct and the choices you have made. And then you become a part of a very complicated situation. That is pretty much what happens to our main character. The whole premise of the story is easy to get pulled into. I could barely put the book down. The story so fluid and so easy to read. I loved every page.<br /><br />The characters were developed so well, and they were so real. My favorite was Wendy. She was raw, real, and strong. She had her own issues, she was not perfect. Those traits make for great characters. The ones that grow with the story. The ones you grow to respect and love. The ones that can teach you a thing or two. I felt like I could become friends with a lot of the characters in this book. I also liked the FC which was The Father's Club. A group of everyday guys fighting their own demons. I loved how I got to learn about each of them throughout the story.<br /><br />There is also a pretty important message in this book even though it is fiction, and that is forgiveness. Something a lot of today's society has a problem achieving. A great quote in this book was "If you hold onto hate you lose your grip on so much more." That speaks volumes to me. I feel that this is a must read book for anyone who loves mystery that keeps you guessing the whole time. This book is a true gem IMO. I have to rate this one a 4.5. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7350830565078445475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SW1w0bSCcz2MP4xWM+lCXgFBrbzbjWi2WETuNej56CduBiKHV9ZjyOpgDaBkL4Qzw9eFSlwrs89pOCM7uR8O3Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wj2JTYlyGCw2h01WTUtp5WwaA+6R5ykge9CaJ1xAxT3lVtsbaiYI2VDYzKAaja+IrowrGBZB8llKrFcpDaYjxw==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/24689.Harlan_Coben">About Harlan Coben</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/24689.Harlan_Coben"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1552500006p3/24689.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>

<a href="/author/show/24689.Harlan_Coben">Harlan Coben

followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2604963703101376158">With over 60 million books in print worldwide, Harlan Coben’s last seven consecutive novels, MISSING YOU, SIX YEARS, STAY CLOSE, LIVE WIRE, CAUGHT, LONG LOST and HOLD TIGHT all debuted at #1 on the <i>New York Times</i> bestseller list and lists around the world. His books are published in 43 languages around the globe.<br/><br/>Coben is the winner of the Edgar Award, Shamus Award and Anthony Award – the first aut</span>
  <span id="freeText2604963703101376158" style="display:none">With over 60 million books in print worldwide, Harlan Coben’s last seven consecutive novels, MISSING YOU, SIX YEARS, STAY CLOSE, LIVE WIRE, CAUGHT, LONG LOST and HOLD TIGHT all debuted at #1 on the <i>New York Times</i> bestseller list and lists around the world. His books are published in 43 languages around the globe.<br /><br />Coben is the winner of the Edgar Award, Shamus Award and Anthony Award – the first author to win all three – and he has received an eclectic variety of honors from all over the world. His novel TELL NO ONE has been turned into a hit French film of the same name. His essays and columns have appeared in many top publications. <br /><br />Harlan was born in Newark, New Jersey. He still lives in New Jersey with his wife, Anne Armstrong-Coben MD, a pediatrician, and their four children.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2604963703101376158" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
